RATING: 9
My absolute favorite sub-10 player count social deduction/hidden role game. It's a logic puzzle with lots of possible different interactions. In particular, I appreciate that there is a timer that short circuits some of the thinking.

Plays surprisingly well at 3/4p and I'd prefer it there over 9-10p almost any day.

RATING: 10
Have racked up most of my plays of this with an experienced group and man it's hard to get the hang of. On the flip side it seems like it might have the most longevity in the genre, but it's best if skill levels are roughly matched. Having one new guy as the lone werewolf can lead to an extremely flat round - speaking from experience! But then again, it's only 10 minutes. 

It also has a surprisingly different feel to anything else in the genre I've played. And I think it'll work well 4p which is a bonus.

edit: it took a long time but I am definitely sold on this. It has a more dynamic, puzzly feel than The Resistance and I definitely think it's worth owning both.

edit 2: Now my clear favourite in the genre and one that only seems to get better and better.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Excellent game. I've always liked werewolf / mafia and its many variants, but this may be the best one yet. What really makes this game stand out is how well the characters play off one another. Every single character In ONUW (except for perhaps the generic villager) adds something interesting to the game. If you find the villagers win too easily in your group, you can add players like "The Minion" and "The Tanner" who can make it more difficult for the villagers. If you find the werewolves are particularly successful, you can throw in "The Hunter" who can potentially trick the werewolves into going after him and still win the game for the villagers. You can make almost endless variants to the rules to play with this deck, as well. 

Overall, ONUW is a very simple easy-to-learn game, with a ton of replay value, and a lot of strategy. Also the app for the game is excellent and allows everyone to play without a "storyteller." About the only complaint I have is that the name is a bit of a mouthful.

RATING: 3
10+ plays / 6,7,8 players

I don't like this game. My first play, I was the only werewolf and wasn't sure what to do. i don't like the feeling of being singled out and accused of things-- which could be some personal psychological problem, but nonetheless, it made my experience uncomfortable.

Plus, trying to lie properly made my adrenaline shoot up and I was too shaky afterwards to play again.

Overall: A bad reaction first play. Tried again weeks later, still didn't like it. The acting and lying is too hard if you aren't given a "role task" to help you (like Avalon for example).

Played two more games, and in both games it felt broken since someone knew who was werewolf right away.

RATING: 6.5
I played this game just three times, so these are mostly impressions that may change after multiple plays.

Being not the biggest fan of social deduction games, I was pleasantly surprised by One Night Ultimate Werewolf. The reason of that being the fact that the game plays very quick and it doesn't take itself too seriously. Many roles in this package in fact are actually very fun to play! Also a considerable improvement over the classic Werewolf is the fact that there's no player elimination in here and everybody is equally involved in the game for the whole time.

Quick, fun little filler game. Nothing extraordinary maybe, but I wouldn't mind to play it again every now and then. Social deduction is still not my cup of tea, but this game is between the ones I enjoy the most of this genre.

RATING: 9
1st plays: Played this 3p 3x in quick succession so I'm only counting it as one play. The game was a lot of fun for a five minute game. I really like these kind of social deduction games, and this one plays VERY fast. The roles provide enough variability and just enough information. 

I love social deduction games but It is very possible that this game gets played out quickly and could drop fast. Then again, that's what I said about Avalon.

2nd plays: played this 6x, tried out the drunk, insomniac and minion. The game is excellent and I'm glad I added it to my order. Fast compact social deduction game with an evolving meta. More depth than I'd expect from such a compact game.

RATING: 2
I despise this game, but I'm not being emotional/contrarian by ranking it a 2.  Let me explain why this is bad:

1. The game loses a lot of nuance by playing it over one night.  You don't get to build off the consequences of your decisions on who to trust.  You can't slow play a betrayal.

2. There are far too many roles.  They don't add much, they confuse people, they lengthen the nighttime phase far too much, and they cause drunken mistakes that ruin games.

3. There are much better hidden-role games that don't require a moderator (resistance and its clones).  Werewolf/Mafia just does.  Without a moderator you miss the slow reveal of who is dying with the chance for elaborate death stories (part of the fun of killing your friends).  You miss a neutral to police things and move the night phase along smoothly.  You need a moderator to know when to force a vote and when to let the debate continue.

4. Oh my, Eric's tone and the way he says "thumbs" makes everyone laugh in a mean way. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
Pros
- Plays quick in about 10-15 mins
- People have to figure out what role they are at the end of the night. Makes for fun conversation. 
- Plenty of roles to change how the game is played each time
- Best with 5 or more
- App is great to be used in the game 
- Same werewolf feel to it
- Lots of lying in the beginning. Truths might appear after. Depends on who wants to lie about stuff. 

Cons
- Hard to coordinate the card switching with bigger numbers like 8-10pm
- Have to be quiet during all the card switching
- Might get a little tricky with all the killing conditions to win if there are a bunch of roles

RATING: 5.5
This is an odd one. It's very streamlined to give you a specific, interesting experience. So in that respect, it should be lauded. But, for me, it's not quite a satisfying experience.

In the first phase - the night - you're effectively just generating the scene of a crime. This is a big elaborate production - if you're using the app - like this is the important/interesting bit of the game. But it isn't. From a practical standpoint, you could just give everyone cards which tell them things that their character knows, and they'd then know what they need to know in 10 seconds, instead of 5 minutes of closed eyes and tapping on the table, waiting. Granted, there might not quite be the experiential impact of having actually done whatever deed or seen whatever information, but personally I don't feel like it would be a major loss, and you could get on to the game faster.

In the second phase, where everyone is trying to deduce what happened during the night, it can be easy for things to devolve into a bunch of people talking all at the same time, and it's hard to keep track of what is going on and what information is revealed. You really sort of need a moderator to run the investigation - but then you're going to win or lose based on what type of character the moderator is. Since it wouldn't work, as the game is, and since there isn't such a role in the game, ultimately the investigation phase is liable to end up as a big blah of noise and confusion.

So, for all the effort the designers put into streamlining the first phase, really I would have preferred they'd spent more effort on the second phase, instead of just burping us up and letting us fend for ourselves, after the night is over.

I wouldn't say that The Resistance is a perfect game, either, but between the two I'd go for that one. You perform the crime in front of everyone, so that part is far more interesting. And since we get/create information gradually over the course of the game, it's less liable to turn into a noise fest of nonsense.

RATING: 8
Great light bluffing game, in the vein of Coup and The Resistance.  A lot more information than in Werewolf, but it ends a lot faster.  You need to get a bit of a feel for which setups are optimal, since certain roles bias towards Werewolves or Villagers but it's generally not too bad.  The relatively high amount of randomness (due to role swapping) is there, but it's a silly five-minute game so it's not too painful.

RATING: 6
One Night Ultimate Werewolf adds a touch more deduction to the basic Werewolf template.  Various characters peek at secret identities and/or re-arrange them.  There is no point in concealing what you saw and did if you think you're not a werewolf.  It also does away with the need for a moderator and gets the whole game played in  less than ten minutes.  This is all quite a feat.  Despite the added deduction, there is still seldom enough information to lynch a werewolf with confidence, so, like its longer cousin, the game does boil down to persuasion.

RATING: 8
After my first play it seems to be at least as good as Avalon especially at the lower player count. The skill of the werewolf can make or break the game. It plays quick so if a game breaks and a werewolf is found out without much of a fight then you can very quickly reset and start again. I'm looking forward to playing this more and finding out if it does manage to take Avalon's place. 

The problems with hearing people moving cards, noticing your card has been moved etc can largely be solved but not entirely eliminated by the app and with some improvisation. 

My initial rating is going to be a shaky 8. I have a feeling it may drop if the wrinkles I found in the gameplay can't be ironed out. Only more plays will clear that up.

RATING: 9.3
Some of my favorite games are hidden role group deduction games (Resistance, Battlestar, Old Werewolf), so this game was right up my alley. I love that they made a free accompanying iPhone app that takes over the moderator role, definitely take the time to get this when you play the game. It was incredibly quick (partially due to low player count) but it still had a lot of strategy. In one game, I was able to convince one of the two other Werewolfs that I had swapped my card with the 3rd player, so we had to kill him. This wasn't the case, but I was able to convince her for the win. It definitely boils down Werewolf in a way that captures its essence without losing the fun. I thought Resistance was a filler game, but this is a filler-filler game; though I still plan to substitute this for regular Werewolf for any group below 11. Highly recommend if you like these type of games.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
[i]Posted: 8/4/17, Rated: 9[/i]

I've been playing [i]Werewolf[/i] on the forums here at BGG since 2004.  It is an amazing game of social deduction and deception, and I made many friends whom I have met in real life at BGG.con as a result.  Still, the most memorable games are the ones which come down to a final three, or some other form of "must win" for the village.  [i]One Night Ultimate Werewolf[/i] basically distills that experience down to a six-minute affair, ending in one vote, winning team takes all.

The idea of having an app be the moderator is a brilliant one, and also one of those "why didn't I think of that?" kind of moments.  The narration by Eric Summerer of Dice Tower fame is perfect (side note: newer versions of the app have added a woman narrator's voice as well, but we still prefer Eric's).  There are plenty of roles to include, and not a whole lot of direction; I suppose the real idea is to just try different things because each game only lasts a few minutes.

Since the game is so quick and balance is left up to the players, I would lean towards giving [i]ONUWW[/i] a rating of "8."  However, it has been a hit with every group to which I have introduced it, to the point where family friends of ours have purchased their own copy, and my son wanted his own to take to college.  A game that approachable deserves an extra point.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
For a long time Resistance: Avalon was the undisputed king of social deduction games for me. Right now it's still the king, but no longer undisputed. One Night Ultimate Werewolf is a very strong contender. One of it's advantages over Resistance: Avalon is the speed of play. You have less time to sow seeds of doubt in your opponents or solve the big puzzle of who is who, but that tends to bring out a different tension entirely and helps to get people talking. Which can sometimes be a problem in Resistance games, where some people end up silent enigmas. The clock is ticking too much for this to happen in ONUW! Plus, the really big difference is you want to figure out what happened to you in the night, because you might not be on the team you think. Which is huge! It turns a "team" type game into a truly individual one. It's absolutely fantastic. The one downside is sometimes it's too easy for the village team to "solve" what happened and correctly out the werewolves. But experience with the game helps, as do different character picks.

[i]Edit[/i]:  Okay, fine. It's equal to Resistance. One is deeper, one is arguably more pure fun.

RATING: 6
When I claimed I was the Troublemaker even though I was the Werewolf. And claimed that I had switched a very convincing Villager for a not all that convincing Villager (in a one villager game), I realized what kind of tricks you could pull off while playing.

However, the game, as with Werewolf, has an awkward start. No one wants to reveal anything because, well, what's the incentive? It's hard to lie when no one has said anything, yet. And there aren't all that many roles where telling the truth is useful.

Unfortunately, the game doesn't become fun until someone reveals something.

The finger pointing at the end is, well, abrupt. Everyone takes an action and then you've won or you've lost.

So, the middle of the game is great, the beginning awkward, and the ending is, well, it ends. Very suddenly.

RATING: 10
I'm kind of shocked by how much I enjoy this game. Going in, I expected Yet Another Social Deduction game, and it sort of is, but honestly, this is probably the one I've had the most fun with. Way more laughs and variety than The Resistance for our group.

There's a fun thing that happens where you're all under the pressure of the time limit (I suggest about 5 minutes with experienced players, 7 for noobs), but nobody wants to be the first to give away information. You want to know for sure which side you're NOW on before you give anything away, and it makes for a lot of fun tension, suspicion, and bluffing.

This functionally works with as little as five, but it gets exponentially more interesting with each added player. Tensions and confusion run REALLY high when you're up to 8 or 9 - as it should be!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
While I’m not a fan of One Night Werewolf, I actually like ONUW quite a lot. There are many more roles, and they are all very interesting. You can mix and match and play with a lot of special power roles, and I always like the customization in a game. Whereas ONW felt random and boring and without any real possibility of deducing, I’ve found that there is actually quite a lot to be deduced in ONUW despite the fact that it only lasts for one night. However, one night doesn’t equal 2-5 minutes, it’s more like 10 in my main group as we tend to try to talk and deduce… Which also means that the werewolves actually lose most of the times! With skilled players, roles like robber and especially troublemaker become very important and can cause great havoc. I haven’t tried each and every one of the roles (think I only need to try out the tanner), and while some work better than others, they are all quite useful. And even if you have a bad/boring role, you can always claim to be somebody else and see what happens…

Sure, sometimes you can get unlucky and have no chance to win (and not even by a fault of your own, but if somebody has switched your role), but that’s the name of the game. It’s so short that you can always just play again! One problem I have with the game is that, with lower player counts, there is a chance for the troublemaker to switch a werewolf and a good guy. When the troublemaker says that, it’s often very hard for the new unawaring werewolf to win… But besides that it’s a good social game.
Oh, and the “lone wolf” optional rule should be the standard rule. Use it!
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
An 8 rating might seem a bit strong, but it's hard to imagine something packing in more entertainment in roughly five minutes. One Night Ultimate Werewolf is strikingly similar to The Resistance. But there are some differences.

One Night is faster, there's only one round of voting, and out of the box you have a dizzying array of different roles. The unique combination of roles is where the fun is found. I give the slight nod to The Resistance because I like the information gained with each round of voting, but this is still pretty slick.

Played it a handful of times with four and with five, and the five player count was noticeably better. I'm thinking this is a 5+ player game.

una nit l'home llop
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
One Night Werewolf was a revelation for how good a game could be with only 8 cards. (It blew Coup and Love Letter away, I think.) Ted takes that great game and expands it in every direction: triple the roles, +4 players, and an incredible iPhone/Android app that solves my only issue with the game, which is it can be difficult to mod and play at the same time. Tokens for helping remember and make deductions are also a nice addition.

The best way I can describe this game is that it is like the players themselves create a puzzle, collectively, but each player only has one little piece of the puzzle.  Collectively they work together to solve the puzzle.  The only complicating factor is that some players can only win the game by ensuring that puzzle isn't correctly solved.  That this can be done in a span of ten minutes is amazing.

Best with 5-7, but is fantastic from 4-8. 9-10 can be hard for logistical reasons (everyone reaching the cards), while 3 seems wonky at first but once you figure out how to play at that count, it too is also amazing.

For a ten minute game, this is easily a 10.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
The resistance distilled for the crowd that wants something a little faster and breezy.

There is only one round, so there is little of the positioning found in similar hidden identity games.  In my few plays thus far, it feels more like you need to make decisions based more on your gut than on the evolving information of the resistance.

However, the fun factor is a little higher on this one.  The throw away feeling allows some really out there play.  People ill make some outlandish claims to watch for reaction, an there is some room for some amazing bluff and doublethink in the short playing time.

I'd still choose the resistance for a more hard-core audience, but the benefit of the throw away nature of this one is that it an be embraced by much younger player (and with those younger players come a whole new helping of deduction).  Whereas I think the resistance begins to shine with a group that has played together multiple times, this one is for the occasional family get-together.

RATING: 10
Awesome game. Definitely best with at least 5-10 players, but still a decent way to play Werewolf if you only have three or four. 

I would say that the game is actually a fairly different experience than a standard game of Werewolf. It's basically the same concept, but it all comes down to defending your position and deducing who is what in one single round, thus making it much more intense. 

I'd also suggest you time the Day phase of the game, thus making coming to a decision more imperative.

RATING: 6.5
This is a really good party game especially when your group is a few drinks in. I rated it at a 6.5 because it doesn't work as well in smaller groups. It ends up being too easy to figure out who the werewolf is or just way too complicated. I usually only end up playing with 4 players and it just isn't as enjoyable at that player count. When you have enough people and the right kind of group, it is a lot of fun. I definitely liked having the app to do the narrating and having the sounds in the background to help drown out some of the noise of moving the cards. The app allows everyone to actually be involved in the game. 
I liked the fact that everyone was involved in the whole game and each round was so quick that you could turn around and play another one really fast, or just use it as a game for the end of the night that isn't as heavy. I would recommend this to anyone trying to get into the board game hobby because that is how I got hooked, or just someone trying to convince their friends that there are more games than just Monopoly.

When you don't have enough time to play Werewolf, you can still play One Night. When people are too tired to play Werewolf, they can still play One Night. When people are in too sour a mood to play Werewolf, they will still be in the mood for One Night. One Night is superior to Werewolf. One Night is one of the best fillers. One Night is one of the best bluffing and social deduction games. Try to prove me wrong, but don't hold me responsible for the wasted time you won't get back, since you can't do it.

Any emotion you care to mention, I can do now thanks to Mr. Ted Alspach.

RATING: 10
Was incredibly excited about this the first couple of times i played it. Now, after 10+ sessions of probably 10+ games per session i'm losing interest. I still rate it an 8 as i think i got more than my money's worth out of it and i'd still play it any time somebody wants to play.

pro: 
fairly quick and simple
great intridcutory game to werewolf/hidden roles/deduction games
Very accessible, i have yet to see a new (casual) player seriously dislike it.

con:
Too random. Too many rounds either provide too much or too little information. Good bluffs become random guesses.
Some rounds become almost auto-wins for either side (2 werewolfs+ minion vs. 3 generic villagers, yeah, it's rare but it happens)

I'd rather play Resistance: Avalon, which takes a bit longer to explain and play but provided more consistent experiences.

And then a couple of months later, after some more plays (because people keep requesting it):

We finally added more roles: minion, tanner, drunk.

BRILLIANT!!!!  JUST SO F****G GOOD!!!!!

We've seriously had some insanely fun game nights with this one! Worth every penny!

If you find it gets boring, check out ALL the other characters!!!!  the Tanner, Drunk and Minion really take it to a new level!!!

RATING: 8
3-10

Er moeten altijd 3 kaarten meer worden gebruikt dan het aantal spelers. Schud de kaarten en geef iedereen gedekt 1 kaart. Iedereen bekijkt in het geheim zijn kaart. De overige 3 kaarten (gedekt) en de fiches van alle karakters in het spel komen in het midden van de tafel.

Gebruik altijd minstens twee weerwolven aangevuld met andere karakters.

Nacht: de verteller/app roept alle karakters 1 voor 1 op. 
Dag: na een paar minuten discussie wordt er gestemd door een andere speler aan te wijzen. 
Het spel is afgelopen na 1 nacht en 1 dag.

Het dorp wint als er minstens 1 weerwolf sterft of als er geen enkele weerwolf in het spel zit en er is niemand gestorven.
De weerwolven winnen als er minstens 1 speler weerwolf is en als er geen weerwolf is vermoord.

Karakters die ’s nachts wakker worden:

1/ Dubbelganger (weerwolfteam of dorpsteam)

De dubbelganger bekijkt ’s nachts de kaart van een andere speler en neemt die rol aan.

2/ Weerwolf (weerwolfteam)

De weerwolf opent ’s nachts zijn ogen en bekijkt welke andere spelers de weerwolven zijn. Als niemand zijn ogen opent, liggen de andere weerwolfkaarten gedekt  in het midden van de tafel. Als er maar 1 weerwolf is, mag hij naar 1 van de gedekte kaarten in het midden van de tafel kijken.

3/ Volgeling (weerwolfteam)

De weerwolven houden hun ogen dicht maar doen hun duim omhoog zodat de volgeling ziet wie de weerwolven zijn. De weerwolven weten echter niet wie de volgeling is. De volgeling behoort tot het team van de weerwolven. Wanneer de volgeling sterft, maar geen enkele weerwolf sterft, dan winnen de weerwolven en de volgeling. Als er geen weerwolven zijn, wint de volgeling als er iemand anders sterft. 

4/ Vrijmetselaar (dorpsteam)

Gebruik steeds de 2 vrijmetselaars. De vrijmetselaar wordt ’s nachts wakker en kijkt of er een andere vrijmetselaar is. Als er geen andere vrijmetselaar is, dan weet hij dat de andere vrijmetselaarkaart gedekt in het midden van de tafel ligt.

5/ Ziener (dorpsteam)

De ziener mag ofwel 1 kaart van een andere speler bekijken ofwel 2 van de 3 kaarten in het midden bekijken.

6/ Dief (dorpsteam)

De dief mag een kaart van een andere speler stelen en zijn diefkaart in de plaats liggen. De speler die de diefkaart krijgt, behoort tot het dorpsteam. De dief behoort tot het team waarvan hij een kaart heeft genomen (hij mag de actie van dat karakter ’s nachts echter niet meer uitvoeren).

7/ Onruststoker (dorpsteam)

De onruststoker mag de kaarten van twee andere spelers met elkaar verwisselen zonder er naar te kijken.

8/ Dronkaard (dorpsteam)

De dronkaard ruilt ’s nachts zijn kaart met een kaart uit het midden van de tafel zonder deze kaart te bekijken. Hij weet dus niet wat zijn nieuwe rol is.

9/ Slapeloze (dorpsteam)

De slapeloze wordt ’s nachts wakker en bekijkt haar eigen kaart (zodat ze weet of haar kaart al dan niet ’s nachts is veranderd).

Karakters die ’s nachts niet wakker worden:

1/ Dorpeling (dorpsteam)

Geen speciale vaardigheid.

2/ Looier (geen team)

De looier wint alleen als hij sterft. Als de looier sterft en er sterven geen weerwolven, dan winnen de weerwolven niet. Als de looier sterft en er sterven ook weerwolven, dan wint het dorpsteam ook (samen met de looier). 

3/ Jager (dorpsteam)

Als de jager sterft, dan sterft de speler die hij aanwijst ook (ongeacht het aantal stemmen).

RATING: 7
This is one of my favorite go-to party games. The game is incredibly simple to teach and learn and the companion app for your phone takes away all the overhead/memorization needed to play it. It takes almost no table space to play so it's great for play around holidays where drinks/food permeate the tabletop and can't be easily cleared.

Some minor caveats that keep the game from being rated higher: There's is very little concrete information to go off of, so many games devolve into baseless accusations (although to be fair, this is half of what makes it fun too). It also may take people some time to acclimate to what all the roles do, making newbie werewolves easy to spot. There's also a tendency for players to give away their roles at night by hearing the rustling of clothes and squeak of chairs. The app tries to mask this with some background music, but realistically it requires all players to commit to doing some light shaking during the night to mask who is moving.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Fluffy little Werewolf variant, played over one night and one day.  Players secretly examine their character then a night phase takes place.  Characters can be examined, swapped, replaced and so on, so when day breaks, things may have changed and players may not be who they initially thought themselves to be.  During the day phase, a free form discussion takes place, where players talk, lie, threaten, cajole, reveal and so on, to try and piece together the puzzle.  Finally, after seven minutes, a vote takes place and a player is lynched.  If it's a werewolf, the villagers win, otherwise the werewolves win.

Fun little 10 minute diversion.  Plenty of roles to blend in and out of the mix.  The victory conditions feel a bit clunky and needlessly complex, making this more a game for gamers.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This was my go-to quick social deduction game for 5 - 7 people. Unlike the Resistance I like that it has an app that takes care of the opening spiel as well as the fact that it has completely divergent play to BSG.  The great thing is that there is no player elimination (I'm looking at you Coup), the game only takes about 10 minutes, and comes with a variety of roles to keep things interesting.  

If I had to knock anything about the game, I would say that rustling sounds during the night phase can ruin things. The trading of roles is also annoying for a few reasons: Tiles are included to make picking up the roles easier, but being that they are tiles, if they get marked the game is ruined. You can sleeve the tiles, but then you have to be more wary of changing the orientation of roles when roles are swapped. Finally, trading is annoying because if people pay attention to where their role card is and it's in a different location when they wake up, they know their role has been swapped and have an advantage.

Don't let these minor issues scare you away from at least trying the game to see if it's right for you.

RATING: 9
One Night Ultimate Werewolf is geared towards less players (including 5-6 players), and consists of just a single round of play, with no player elimination or moderator.

It has two additional characters dealt to the middle of the table, to add some uncertainty to the mix. Of the special characters in the game, one role is a robber, who secretly switches another role with his own, and a trouble-maker, who secretly switches two other roles.

This makes deduction possible, but it will be thwarted by the deception of any werewolves that are present... 

It's not completely a guessing game: if everyone told the truth, you'd have enough information to deduce all the roles.  Problem is, at least one person is probably lying... and that's where the fun comes in!  (but do non-werewolves have any incentive to lie?)  

This mixture of bluffing & deduction sounds exactly like the kind of micro-game I enjoy immensely.

See my pictorial review: http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/1069101

Probably best with 5, but good for 4-8; 9-10 becomes logistically difficult.  See also: [thread=1077621][/thread]

Also owned: the expansion [gameid=163166]

RATING: 9
I still don't understand why this game works as well as it does, but it somehow manages to. You go to bed at night after looking at your power and then wake up in the morning after everybody has exercised their power during the night phase. The thing is, somebody might have used their power to switch your card and you wouldn't know it. That shouldn't work, but somehow it does because it creates situations for people to either give the village information or lie and obfuscate things.

It's definitely a hard road to hoe as the bad guys though. If you're a wolf or minion, you better be ready to have a bogus story to sell upon wakeup. My group is seeing a lot of overly bad play by the minion to die and take one for the team which provides some nice double-think.

Update: Nowhere near as good as the real thing, but it has its niche -- a large group but not a lot of time. We have a lot of fun with this one and have found the less time the better b/c things get crazier with time running out. With more than, say, 5 minutes, the village usually is able to figure things out. So less is more here.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.8
This game has the potential to breed some of the most hectic-fun, mind-boggling, and satisfying experiences! I've had many many incredibly exciting moments and memories playing this game! At its best no one trusts anyone besides themselves(even that isn't ensured) and there is no way to be sure of what really happened, alongside an exhilarating adrenaline rush increasing until the final moments. After the reveal holds either incredible triumph or a still-confusing defeat; in either case, my favorite part is the potential, prolonged chatter and discussion about the game, sometimes lasting longer than the game itself!
Although, at its worst, there is little excitement. All too often there is no question over which character is which. No unsureness. No satisfaction. Everyone votes for the same player and the reveal is quiet. This can be due things going to smoothly, randomly, or the culprit is the group you are playing with. If there are a few or multiple people who aren't invested at all, it somehow often ruins the whole game. No one has a reason to disagree or lie because no one cares! This can be a huge issue for me, although I don't think that its entirely the game's fault! Almost every game suffers when the players don't care. Overall, I have loved my time with this game, despite the mundane rounds! Great quick game for a big group! (Most of my plays have been with the Daybreak expansion too, which I recommend you pick up along with the base game.)

RATING: 8
Have played with up to 8 people.
This game is very simple to learn and the rounds go by quick, so after just 20 minutes of playing you should have a few rounds under your belt, and a great understanding of the mechanics.  The phone app you use will walk you through each step to avoid any confusion.

Perfect game to start a night of board games, or to bring new players into new styles of games to play.  It's a very party friendly game and as there is almost no explanation necessary you can get new players up to speed in minutes.  

My only suggestion to people looking into this game would be to play with at least 5, and not use the specialty cards right out of the gate!

RATING: 8.3

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
One Night Ultimate Werewolf has proven to be one of the most popular games within my various gaming circles. It isn't the best game in my collection, but it's certainly one of the most accessible. 

+ There is minimal setup time.
+ The app removes any need for a moderator.
+ Short game length leads to many quick games, variety to the roles each player gets to experience, and a rapidly changing meta-game. 
+ The rules are easy to explain, but...

- ...teaching basic strategy to new players can prove difficult, particularly in the context of changing roles after the night phase. Several individuals that I've played with have struggled to figure what exactly they need to be doing in order to win.
- Teaching many new people at once leads to relatively boring games, at least until they figure out how beneficial it can be to lie, misinform, etc.
- It can take some time to figure out good character setups. Be careful to keep the balance between werewolves and villages stable.

RATING: 5

Oh well, it was worth two rounds, but I can't imagine wanting to play this again. Would much rather play Coup.

RATING: 5
I enjoy playing this game with a group of 6-8 players. Art is beautiful, the game is fun, fast paced, messy, easy to teach and great for family. 
However, I have observed that newbies struggle to feel when to bluff and when to tell the truth. In the other hand, with confirmed players, it gets impossible to tell if someone is bluffing or telling the truth. In fact, so much bluff gets into it that it gets very hard to have a strategy, preventing the game from being deep.
It has some early replayability as you choose different characters each game. But as people get to know how to play, replayability runs out as people bluff well, the game gets too messy to make anything out of the new characters in play.
Finally, the game can either suffer from Quarterbacks taking control of the discussion or the discussion can get also super messy - either way is not cool.

RATING: 7
An interesting take on the Werewolf/Mafia style of game. Everything takes place over one night, so really this comes down to one big argument over who's telling the truth about who they were at the start, and what they got up to when everybody's eyes were closed. Roles can be swapped, replaced, or spied on, and some have additional win conditions.

I'd say the app for this is almost essential as it handles all the stuff about who has to open their eyes in what order, so nobody has to referee things.

Having to make a bit of noise to obscure people moving tokens around is a bit odd, but you get used to it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Excellent party game.  


Players start with some information and allegiances.  Things are then potentially changed through the chaos of the secret night actions.  Players then use lies, half-lies and the odd bit of truth to figure out not only what happened but also which team they are on.  This is followed by a flurry of finger pointing and players checking to see if they have won.  It is quick, fun and offers a rich thematic induction/bluffing experience.

I love how there is this layer of pressure, created by the chaos, that forces the players to engage each other.  Not only is the engagement necessary but It adds to the tension/theme.

I can see how this game might fall flat if a group fails to engage and adopts an overly rigid understanding of how to play.  This game really rewards creativity, deduction and flexibility.  It is pretty much exactly what I want in a party game.

RATING: 4
The game works remarkably better than its predecessor Werewolf. There is room for bluffing and deduction. The time limit (when using the app--which I highly recommend), creates a lot of tension.

There is a flaw in the game, however. And it is almost a fatal flaw. I'm docking the game 3 points because of it. The flaw: you have to swap cards on the table while everyone else has their eyes closed. Even when one's eyes are closed, you can still sense movement from your neighbors. This gives away your opponent's role. And this makes the game ultimately flawed. 

I do not see any way around this flaw either. The card swapping is integral to the game. Detecting movement from around the table is inevitable.

RATING: 8
Awesome implementation of the well-known werewolf game. 

The two mechanics here are deduction & bluffing, nothing more nothing less.

It's much quicker, there's no player elimination, got cool artwork, funny characters, scales perfectly with different player numbers.. (although with greater numbers the night/downtime increases).. great party game, a keeper.

The downloadable App facilitates playing greatly!

Handles player numbers rather well, from 3 all up to 10.. with 10 you should use the app though..

The thing i just recently realized is that once you understand the game & roles, not is it only about reading other players but also to fabricate valid arguments.. like: if this is true than this must be true, then he must lie, then i actually became a werewolf, so i have to present that player a valid argument why he should vote for that person to be killed.. incredibly good!

This shouldn't work.  It shouldn't!  And yet...

I won't be counting individual plays, but rather [i]entire sessions[/i]—it's so quick we never play it fewer than a bunch of times in a sitting!

Also:  The free app is pretty sweet—it runs through the whole script (based on the roles in play), makes atmospheric background noises to cover the inevitable shuffle of cards, and has a configurable countdown timer which then calls for the vote.

Includes:  [thing=163166]Daybreak[/thing]

RATING: 6
Neutral - on occasion.

Play few 5[ games so far. Overall interesting, but there are few bad things that can happen in a game:

(1) Characters that are able to switch, or with a possible change from one side to another, will constantly create an almost random game.

(2) It's pretty common, at the very beginning of the day(i.e. the final identity is already set), one side has actually no hope, and the whole game is all about discovering that, quite frustrating. This core problem comes from the luck of drawing characters, and I wish the rules could recommend some good-enough combination of characters, rather than let players test by themselves.

I know it's extremely short, but these things happen too frequently to be annoying. Also, some characters' abilities are over-complex for a 5-minute game. But it's minor, players can play few times and get familiar with them.

RATING: 7
I'm not big on social inference games but for this genre this is pretty good.  It is an improvement on the classic werewolf game where everyone is the villager except for the hidden werewolf folks are getting eaten one at a time until they figure out who is doing it.  Instead of player elimination and resulting boredom there is only one chance to figure out who is the werewolf.  To make this work, most of the players have special abilities (like secretly switching two role cards) which gives them more info and more grounds to bluff.  There are lots of different roles with different abilities which provides good replayability.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Make some role cheat sheets and use the available app to run the game and this can be a solid choice as a large party game where people can drop in-and-out as desired.

2014-04-18

Initial Rating: 6.5 (April 2014)

As I love werewolf, it is no surprise I like this game. It has great components and the free app is a stroke of genius. I expected a different game (more control) and for that I’m a bit disappointed, still very fun when you get to play the robber or the troublemaker, they add a Mascarade feel to the game.

You no longer need a moderator to play Werewolf which is GREAT! This was the only thing I really hated (to be) in the previous version of the game.

This is still the same core game (which has tons of luck) but now the player elimination is not a problem, also it plays lightning fast (5 minutes or less). For some reason I prefer the longer version of the Ultimate Werewolf game, here I feel (most of the time) I have no control or idea who is the werewolf. In the longer game there are more opportunities to catch them. Still very similar games and I enjoy both of them.

It is a great werewolf game to play with fewer players than the original, for this reason I will keep both in my game collection. I must be the only one that prefer the long version of the game.

Current Rating: 6.5
[hr]
2014-05-01

After more plays, I continue to like the game. Still I’m considering selling it as I’m not sure I need both werewolf games in my collection. Besides with the Ultimate Werewolf components I can play this version of the game too. I’m still undecided about this, perhaps I will keep both. I usually don’t take part in the philosophy that a game replaces another game, but in this case both games are very similar.

The short playtime is definitely a turn off for me, but most friend love this aspect of the game. I spend more time explaining the game than playing it. 

Current Rating: 6.0

[b][url=https://boardgamegeek.com/thread/1317685/2014-golden-geek-awards-nominees-announced-vote-no]2014 Golden Geek Nominee[/url][/b]

One Night Ultimate Werewolf is a fast game for 3-10 players in which everyone gets a role: One of the dastardly Werewolves, the tricky Troublemaker, the helpful Seer, or one of a dozen different characters, each with a special ability. In the course of a single morning, your village will decide who is a werewolf...because all it takes is lynching one werewolf to win!

Players: 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8, 9, 10
Time: 10 min
Mechanics: [property=2028][/property], [property=2015][/property], [property=2017][/property]
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
This is a pretty good hidden role game. It's almost like a mashup of Werewolf and Mascarade. It has a very chaotic element where you may or may not actually know who you are. I wouldn't mind that at all, but we had two games in a row where the troublemaker started off by telling everyone who they switched, which allowed one of me to then say, "Well, I was a werewolf, so now they must be." It blindsided the other player, who obviously had no defense. Of course, that shouldn't happen that often, but it still felt a little broken. It seems like the Troublemaker should have some kind of incentive to keep their mouths shut, at least for a little while. Still, it's a fast game, so it doesn't ruin it at all. Still a good time.

Update: After more plays, this game has really started to shine. The trick is getting to the point where players are ready for anything to happen (previous Werewolf experience can help with this). Once you get there, this game is a lot of fun. It has bluffing and deduction and a lot of the feel of regular Werewolf, but in a nice, fast playing package.

Another update: Bumping this up to an 8. This game is really just fantastic.

This is a great way to open a night of spooky gaming.

RATING: 10

RATING: 5
Obviously this is not regular Werewolf: instead of a gradual stream of information and escalating tension, here you have a quick reveal and recursive mapping of the game state. The problem is that once this narrative of game events is established you may find yourself with a brand new incentive to change it, yet without any credible argument for doing so. This won't happen to every player in every game, but it may happen to some player in every game. Playing online was fun in a "wacky speed chatting" way more than in an... "actual gameplay" way. Probably better suited for tabletop play than play-by-forum, and likely preferable to Werewolf that way for many.

RATING: 8.2
The best thing about this game: You can experiment and do crazy stuff without risk, because even if you fail the next game starts within 5 minutes and so it doesn't really matter. In real werewolf or other games if you make a mistake you lost like 20min, 30min or even more of playing time, so you can't risk a failure and you have to play safe. This one you can play really stupid and really risky turns and it doesn't matter.

Artwork and components and everything is excellent.

Some games are really lots of fun. A few games sometimes are not that much fun.

Well, I still love it a lot :-) :-) :-)

RATING: 5
No moderator, no elimination, ten-minute games.

One Night Ultimate Werewolf is a fast game for 3-10 players in which everyone gets a role: One of the dastardly Werewolves, the tricky Troublemaker, the helpful Seer, or one of a dozen different characters, each with a special ability. In the course of a single morning, your village will decide who is a werewolf...because all it takes is lynching one werewolf to win!

Really wanted to like this game, but it lacked structure. Will have to try with more people (5+) and see if the game improves.

RATING: 7
A game about deception and deduction. Each player plays a character in a village that inhabits some werewolves. The goal for the villagers is to find and hang just one werewolf, while the werewolves are trying to hide and survive. The game requires a lot of tabletalk and each player should be comfortable about lying. 5+ players recommended. 

Replay Value: 4
Difficulty: 2, due to the amount of roles
Time: 5-10 minutes

RATING: 9.25
Absolutely fantastic party game that is endlessly replayable. Cannot recommend more. Anyone can learn it. The iOS/Android apps are highly recommended, if not necessary, as it saves someone from having to be the announcer and therefore adds another player. Doesn't get dragged down with the max players, like most games. Can be played as a filler, can be played as a main game, can be played as a starter, can be played as a finisher, can be played once, can be played 20 times, can be played with 3 players (though I prefer an absolute minimum of 4), can be played with 10 players, can be played with newbies, can be played with experts. Just a splendid board game.

RATING: 6
Like the social deduction game Werewolf, a village must find and lynch the werewolves that haunt their town, but the game takes place all in one night! To add complexity, various roles can cause strange happenings meaning people's identities and allegiances may switch without them knowing it. Are you still a werewolf? Is the player across from you lying about being a troublemaker and switching your partner's role. You have 5 minutes to decide in this fast game of lies.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
If I actually was a fan of social deduction games, this would rate a lot higher, as this is very excellently designed. Distills the best of the genre into 10 minutes without need of player elimination or loss of werewolf's characteristic plethora of special powers. How these powers interact depending on what roles are left out and who has what is also quite interesting, and that you can change up which roles you play with and different roles are added/left out with different number of players mean that even if you play with the same people over and over, each game won't feel the same, something that can't be said about Resistance (and to a lesser extent Coup).

RATING: 4
Probably the most surprising plummet in the ratings for me, I initially had it up much higher and then kept moving it down as other things overtook it. I think it's time to accept that I'm not as much of a fan as I used to be of one night. In fact, I even cancelled my Aliens Kickstarter pledge because I don't want another One Night expansion sitting on my shelves unplayed.

It's not that this isn't a solid game. It's that there is ALWAYS a game I would rather play. Shadow Hunters has effectively punted it out when I want a quick social deduction game because of everything it has going on, and I'll never want to play One Night over Werewolf.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
My favorite party game for mid-sized (6ish) groups. Larger? Telestrations. Smaller? Um. Er. I don't know that "3-player party game" is a niche that [i]needs[/i] to be filled, but it's one that I haven't filled. Daybreak is OK (but more complicated), Vampire looks more complicated still. I think this one is the sweet spot.

The secret to this game (says the guy who's not at all sure he's really learned the secret to this game) is to be the first player to credibly claim a knowledge role that happens to be in the unused pool. Sometimes that's guesswork, and sometimes it's knowledge, but being able to lie without anyone being able to contradict you is how you out your opponents.

Standard Werewolf is a game that I've never gotten into, but saw this one on sale and decided to give it a go.  Really great decision on my part.  The "one night" format lends itself to quick gameplay and as a result, you're starting fresh in just a matter of minutes.  Compared to other werewolf games I've seen, this also lends itself to an element of deduction that I haven't seen in other versions of Werewolf that I've seen.  I kid you not, we played this twenty times straight with a small break in the middle...that's how great this was.   One bit of advice, play with the Minion card.  It helps complicate things in a  good way when you have the Troublemaker in play.  Highly recommend using the app to guide you through the instructions!

RATING: 6
One of the better short-form social deduction games if you are looking for games strictly on social information instead of deduction information (e.g. the pass/fail cards in the Resistance)

Personally, I dislike the original werewolf because of its long play length and player elimination.  ONUW fixes this problem by boiling the game down to 10 minutes with no player elimination.

Because of this, just having social information is acceptable.  If you get the Daybreak expansion, you have a game with an insane amount of replay value.

That being said, in a large group (7-12) there really isn't a better game that I can think of playing. Plus it plays really quick so I'll usually play a couple rounds if everyone else is into it.

RATING: 6
This feels like it needs another play or two to click -- I can see a better-than-a-7 game here -- but unfortunately at least a couple of folks in my group didn't enjoy it at all. It's as fast as advertised, and the app makes things so easy (and I love not having to have a narrator, or forgetting things). The one-night twist delivers as advertised.

It feels like the first night/day of regular Werewolf in some ways, though -- the day in which no one's quite sure how to kick things off. It's so quick that you can safely throw caution to the wind and just get it over with, and then play again, but there's something a bit unsatisfying about that at the same time. I liked it, and I'll happily play it again if the opportunity arises.

---

My group couldn't stand this and I don't know who else I'd play it with, and I like it less than vanilla Werewolf or other fast-playing games, but my wife wants to keep it. Re-rated from a 7 to a 6.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.5
Awesome game! One Night Ultimate Werewolf has so many things going for it: great art, great components (thick tiles rather than cards are really nice), play in less than 10 minutes, and most importantly, it's A LOT of fun. It's loud, fast and furious. Our group played 16 games in one sitting! Those 16 games took a little over 3 hours. I tried comparing this game to Resistance: Avalon, which is difficult, because despite their similarities in style, they play out very differently. All things considered, I like them equally. 

Update 2/16/14:

This game is the f*cking business! I have played 34 times in 2 sittings. If ratings were based on how addictive a game is, this would be tops! I literally can't say one bad thing about it. At this point, I'd have to give the nod to this over Avalon.

Update 4/21/14: 

Played this at Easter with family. I still had a lot of fun, and it was still a hit for the most part, but it wasn't near as much fun with a diverse group (broad range in age and gaming experience). Despite being an excellent "party game," it is still, at its heart, a strategy game. IF YOU HAVE PEOPLE IN YOUR GROUP WHO EITHER DON'T LIKE TO PLAY THE WEREWOLF OR DON'T PLAY IT WELL, THIS GAME BECOMES QUITE UNBALANCED. I'm not going to take that away from the game though. I will say that I'm lowering my rating ever so slightly because the tiles scar easily.

RATING: 10
Best game of 2014.
This game is GREAT. So. Much. Fun. It's way easier to teach than any other social deduction game. Good gateway to genre. Just pick very basic roles for first game (rulebook has a suggestion), do one round (maybe with shorter timer, 3min is good) and everyone will be all set. Games take 6 minutes but offer just as much fun as longer deduction games. It's also more light-hearted than something like Resistance. I'm by no means dissing Resistance, it's one of my favorite games too, but I'm fan of the slight chaos this one offers. No moderator (if you don't happen to own Android device or iPad or whatever you'll need one player to speak the commands, but he can still play - if you do own one, then I must mention that the app is very well-made and had way more customization than I expected), no player elimination, great components, good replayability. And did I mention it's always FUN. 

Update: Amazing achievement. Perfect game. This one has quickly become one of my favorite games of ALL TIME. It's the game I'll suggest every single time I have opportunity to play with 4 or more other players. 

Expansions:
+One Night Ultimate Werewolf: Daybreak
+One Night Ultimate Werewolf: Bonus Pack 1 & 2

RATING: 6
I've played Mafia / Werewolf plenty while growing up, and while this game lacks the narrative, the fun storytelling and the gradual build-up of suspicion and drama that happens when you are playing a 10+ person game of regular Werewolf, it condenses it and strengthens the deduction element. When you play you weave these long trains of thoughts, explicit facts, uncontested and contested statements, bald faced lies and then you try to untangle what they imply. Or you are a stinky liar yourself, and try to ride the wave of building suspicion so you can gently steer it to anyone but you (or your team, or maybe you want it to land squarely on you you filthy Tanner!).

Sure, you all look a bunch of dummies when everyone is tapping their hand on the table to cover the noise, as the app drones on about which role does what, but do you care? No. The game is fun, can be played by anyone who doesn't mind lying (of which there are some, strange people), and the variety of roles and setups you can roll with mean you can try out strange things causing wildly different outcomes and discussions.

A great game!

RATING: 6
Gets many things right that are problematic with normal werewolf, mafia, vampire etc.

The free app replace the moderator, there is only one round, so no-one is eliminated while the game runs, and discussion can easily be limited to say 5 minutes.

Downside for me is that the switching of roles is highly unthematic. How exactly did she turn the insomniac into a werewolf? Also, some people seem prone to lie about everything, claiming that this gives them insights, which makes the discussion a mess. 

Still, if I have to play werewolf etc. then it would be this or its one-night cousins.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Few games have earned so many plays in so little time as this one, mostly because it's very available and very short, and almost demands multiple plays each time it hits the table. It's chaotic and silly but it works for me. Most notedly, it works where Resistance fails, as I feel they are going after the same goal. It can be a little difficult to jumpstart, but once someone gets talking, you are able to garner more real data than in either Resistance or Werewolf, so it isn't quite so replete with blind accusations. Skill comes into play with clever lies, which must be different depending on your actual role, your perceived role, and your projected role. Those lies can direct, misdirect, or fish for information. This is the only traitor game I've liked so far, and I love how fast it plays!

RATING: 8
This game hits my table more than just about anything.  The entire family loves it.  It plays fast, under 7 minutes but the fun factor is fantastic.

It is very much like regular werewolf but a bit more casual since it is over so soon.  If they vote you out it is no big deal since you can play it again right away.  No elimination.

Just had a game where we voted out my daughter who thought she was a villager and she angrily turned over her card to discover she was the tanner and had just won the game.  Absolutely hilarious.  Moments like that make this game priceless.

The app makes it so much more wonderful.  So good to have the app narrate for you so you don't forget anything and so that everyone gets the same amount of time to do their nightly activities.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
[b]Like:[/b]
-Outsmarting your opponents with lies
-The moment you realise you're actually on another team than you thought you were
-Very easy to teach, especially since it's really similar to the well known regular Werewolf game
-Lovely art!

[b]Dislike:[/b]
-Disruptable and sometimes long night phase
-Getting the goal of the game across to new players quickly might lay in the hands of luck

Excellent game! It checks all my boxes: funny, bluffing, outplaying... It's so easy to explain, very flexible playtime, and adjustable roles to fit any kind of player. It has one of the best moments in gaming ever: when you realise in the middle of a discussion you're actually working for the other team...

I find only two (very small) negatives:
1) the night phase can be a bit too long and susceptible to interruption. 
2) the first game with new people can be a bit underwhelming since you can't guarantee every role is in the current game (like the important werewolves or role-switchers). You just have to tell them to trust you that this was indeed a bad role-distribution but by that time they may not want to try again anymore (hasn't happened to me yet though since it's only 5 minutes, but I can see it happen).

Self-evidently, you also need to be pretty good at lying. If the Troublemaker tells you you've been switched with another person and that other person says he was a Werewolf, if you just give up then and there it will be unexciting. You can say for example you were the Seer and know the self-declared Troublemaker isn't really a Troublemaker, and if you already revealed yourself earlier as someone else, you can say you just said that to bust other people.

RATING: 6.5
This is Werewolf played in one round. Some of the original roles from the game are there, but other roles are added. You negotiate for 10 minutes, then lynch another player, and depending on the role of the villager lynched, villagers or werewolves win. 

I like this better than the original Werewolf, since it is much cleaner, since the original game could be protracted with players eliminated having to sit and wait. I wasn't a huge fan of the original Werewolf; this game makes it quick and fun, over in one round.  Good to play at the end of a game session.

RATING: 9
My favorite micro-game, bumping For Sale off. This has as few cards as games like Love Letter and Coup, yet it has the espionage and intrigue of Resistance, and it has different characters and unexpectedly high variability.

I love the bluffing that happens in this game and its tremendous fun even losing when you discover you're not actually the role you expected.
Hopefully the app stays good though.
The closest comparison would be a single, intense mission round of Resistance, but ONUWW's faster playtime is a huge plus. 

One small issue I have is that players have to crowd around a table a bit (helps if you stand), which gets difficult especially at higher player counts. Also, a small physical issue I have is that keeping my eyes closed so long sometimes annoys me (but this is just a minute physical tick).
Another thing is that the cards could've had the effects written on them alongside the roles and also higher quality tiles without wear.
I don't usually like chaotic games, but since this one's so short, I don't mind. Its the best werewolf game I've ever played too (so far).

Overall great party/light deduction game thats similar to a mini-Resistance of sorts. BTW, I recommend getting the announcer app too!

Plays: Many (estimated 10-20?)

RATING: 8
I hate Werewolf. It's just a terrible reskin of Mafia, and because the people I've played with get bored, they often kill randomly and quickly so the games will go fast and they won't be out too long if they're eliminated.

One Night Werewolf solves all of these problems. The game is fast, no one is excluded, the roles are interesting, and they lead to fun logical messes. I've only played this game at one gaming night so far, but we played about ten games in just an hour, and it was a good hour of fun.

I really think the BGG community is right when saying it plays better from 4-10. Certain roles like the troublemaker can be really random but luckily the game comes with so many other roles to swap in.

RATING: 3
6 plays - A well designed game, but just not my cup of tea. This is really not a game for beginners, as opposed to many other secret identity games. All the different 'roles' almost always confuse people. This is particularly noticeable when you try to lie about your role. Usually a beginner's lies will not make sense, as they confuse the roles, and say things that aren't actually possible, sending immediately obvious signals to others. Further, the amount of chaos that is caused by the different roles is (in my opinion) ridiculous. My idea of fun, is trying to figure out people's identities while hiding my own. If people aren't even aware of their own roles though (because they've been switched by another player for e.g.), then figuring out roles is just annoying, and a chaotic mess. I'm sure with some groups who understand the game well, they can work together to figure out who is who, but with all the groups I've played with, at least half the people are just lost and have no idea. I much prefer games like the resistance, where lying isn't so complicated, and people can have fun without all the role confusions. I'd rather not try to piece together a jigsaw puzzle, and simply try to bluff and call other people's bluffs. I just want to play a game about lying, manipulation and deceit, I don't want to enroll in a logic course.

RATING: 7
A nice fifteen minute version of the original. It is one round and the android app really helps as you do not need anyone guiding the game. You spend one night where characters can move cards around and then 10 minutes trying to kill off a werewolf if you are human or trying to kill off a human if you are a werewolf. There is not that many options so the discussions are limited, but if you want a quick versatile game, it is worth a look.

The app seemed to work okay, but it was a little boring waiting for everyone else to make your move while you had to keep your eyes closed.

RATING: 10
Absolutely phenomenal social deduction game, the best of the best. Most social deduction games fall flat for our group, because people feel bad about betraying their friends, because there's nothing to deduce at the start, and because you have to play them a few times to get good them. One Night Ultimate Werewolf solves all of these problems because it's short enough to play consecutively, there's no player elimination, you get ALL the information right away, and everybody's equally invested until the last 5 seconds!!

RATING: 10
(50+ plays) I had a great first experience playing this game with a group of strangers.  It's an extremely fast, highly interactive social deduction game - and a total blast to play.  If you know Mafia or Werewolf, this game will be easy to learn.  It has the advantage of a fixed game length of around 10 minutes, no moderator, and no player elimination.  I believe they may have designed the perfect formula for this style of game.  Now, after playing a bunch of games with a wide variety of different people - family, friends, colleagues, strangers... this is my favorite new game.

Quick and clever, there are some devious twists that make this a different experience than Werewolf (for instance, you can begin the game a villager and become a werewolf.  And not even know it!).  This will appeal to families and groups that don't like all the arguing/intrigue of Werewolf, but for my money nothing beats a knock-down-drag-out full game of Werewolf.

RATING: 8

This changes all of that.

RATING: 8
ONUW is a wonderful game of lying and deduction that quite literally takes only 15 minutes to play.

However those 15 minutes will be some of the most interesting, confusing, and hilarious few minutes you'll have for a long time.
Imagine all of the deduction, teamwork, lying, and frenzy of Werewolf/Mafia, without any of the tension, hostility, or player elimination that usually drives people away.

ONUW is amazing.  Absolutely perfect for parties, and introducing non-gamers into our world.

RATING: 6
The game seems fun for a few minutes but after a while, it is a bit stale. There are usually a few players in the game who must absolutely lie about who they are (their character) and the rest of the players simply tell the truth and try to make sure that anyone else telling the truth believes them. Yes, it's fun when someone gets away with their lie and everyone went for it. But when you end up as a villager for three or four games in a row, there's just nothing to do but wait and see if someone thinks you are lying - then you must argue that you are being truthful with little to nothing to back up your claim. It's sort of like arguing with people about politics and religion sometimes.

But for the first few plays at a party with new people, it's worth playing.

RATING: 9
The best of the social deduction games.  So much fun packed in 10 minutes.  Sometimes a setup will result in a dud game (too easy to deduce a werewolf too quickly), but the games go so quick it doesn't matter, just play again.  

The last game we played, my buddy and I were werewolves and together we pulled off such a convincing deception, we couldn't resist a high-five after the reveal.  We had no collusion before the game or anything, but we were so in synch with the deception it felt as if we planned it ahead of time even though it was completely off the cuff and improvised. Our lies supported each other and had almost everyone else convinced the werewolf was the guy sitting to my buddy's right.  The guy we accused wasn't even sure himself because I claimed to be the troublemaker and swapped their cards. It felt borderline telepathic.  Great stuff!

One of the most satisfying gaming experiences in such a small box.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 10
One Night is without a doubt one of my favorite games. The group I play with is a big fan of games like The Resistance, which I personally think has grown a bit repetitive after so many plays. I picked this up looking for a fresh take on the hidden roles game, and I've always been a fan of mafia games like Werewolves.

Our first play was hilariously one-sided, as we were all so used to hidden roles games no one wanted to share anything, but we quickly fell into the game's groove, playing dozens of 5-10 minutes rounds until well past 4 in the morning.

The plays we've seen have been amazing. Playing werewolves feels like skipping ahead to that tense final round of The Resistance when everything is revealed. We've seen the troublemaker claim to switch player's roles, at which point a werewolf immediately tries to finger the new wolf, thinking they're now on the town team, only for the troublemaker to reveal they lied about who they switched seconds later. We've caught players in carefully calculated lies and lynched them only to hang the tanner. I've had games where I thought I was a werewolf, trying my hardest to throw a townsperson under the bus, and succeed, only to discover I was no longer the wolf afterwards and had just handed the game to my buddy, who I thought I had managed to convince I was right. The list of crazy plays goes on. One of the best things is watching one player jump up declaring victory, only to flip their card and see they actually lost.

This game has far more staying power than Resistance in my book. The variety of roles and the ability to switch them out keeps things fresh. My group has easily played over a hundred rounds by now (which is rather easy, seeing as a session takes only a few minutes, especially if narrated by the convenient iOS/android app), and have started mixing things up. In our most recent game, we were playing with 4 players. We had no seer, just to see how it would work, instead using all the town roles that gave information; the masons, robber, troublemaker, insomniac, etc.

We've played 4 players games with only one werewolf and a minion, which work out great. It's always hilarious when there's a minion in play and the werewolves are in the middle, as the only way the minion can win is if someone, anyone in town dies, even themselves. We've even had a game where the minion and wolves outnumbered the village 3-2, and the wolves (and minion) won by all voting the minion.

Bottom line, this is one of the best games you can pull out for 3-12 (really, the sweet spot is around 5-8, but 3-12 is still a great game). It's a fantastic, fast game to play while waiting for another member of your group, but you may end up continuing to play well after they arrive. It's a surprisingly easy game to spend an entire evening on. I really cannot recommend this game enough to just about any kind of group, especially as it's price.

Protip: once you're used to it, try playing without the tokens. Things get really crazy when players can't look at the token bank to see what's left to claim.

RATING: 7
I can't figure out for sure whether I like this game, but so far I've enjoyed playing it.  There are definitely less bad feelings from lying or being lied to in this compared to a game like The Resistance.

If all of the town-aligned players (before nightfall) tell the truth, then the game is easily solved and the wolves will lose.  Once townies figure out that they have to lie too (and they will the moment they begin the game town and switch overnight), the game really opens up.  It feels like it comes down to a coin flip or gut call most games.  There are two (or more) consistent narratives and you just have to choose one and vote!  So deduction takes a back seat to reading players.

The more advanced roles make the deductions harder but do so at the cost of a much longer setup time.

RATING: 6
-kurze Spieldauer 
-würde es ab 6 Personen empfehlen
-Kartenspiel
-Partyspiel
-jeder schlüpft in eine Rolle

Vorab: ich kenne das Original Werwölfe nicht.

Jeder zieht eine verdeckte Karte und nimmt in der Nachtphase die entsprechende Rolle ein.
Dort müssen alle Spieler ihre Augen geschlossen halten und wenn sie an der Reihe sind, dürfen sie je nach Rolle eine Aktion ausführen.
In der darauffolgenden Tagphase wird diskutiert.
Die Dorfbewohner (unterschiedliche Charaktere) müssen dafür sorgen, dass ein Werwolf bei der abschließenden Abstimmung die meisten Stimmen erhält( somit angeklagt wird). Die Werwölfe gewinnen, wenn keiner von Ihnen verdächtigt wird.
Einige Rollen modifizieren die Regeln etwas. 
Ein Günstling z. B. gewinnt, wenn die Werwölfe gewinnen.
Ein Gerber ist suizidgefährdet und gewinnt, wenn er verdächtigt wird. 

Es ist also Sinn des Spiels, dass man je nach Rolle andere verdächtigt und entsprechend argumentiert.
Es wird geflunkert um ggf. von sich abzulenken oder um den Verdacht absichtlich auf sich zu ziehen -  nach dem Prinzip "wenn Du denkst, denkst,dass ich denke...".

In der richtigen Runde kann es sehr unterhaltsam sein.

Dies ist für Personen mit folgenden Charakterzügen nicht zu empfehlen:
-nachtragend
-mit großer Hemmschwelle davor, darauf loszuflunkern.

Ein weiters Problem gibt es meiner Meinung nach, wenn gewisse Spieler zu dominant und andere zu zurückhaltend sich an der Diskussion beteiligen.

In der richtigen Gruppe ab 6 würde ich dem Spiel eine höhere Wertung geben.
Wir haben allerdings gehofft, daas es sich auch zu viert oder fünft besser spielen lässt.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
I love social deduction: the classic Werewolf game was my gateway into the world of board gaming, and it’s still a favourite among my friends; yet, One Night Ultimate Werewolf bores me to no end. Essentially, One Night strips down Werewolf to its bare components while adding an almost absurd amount of randomness into the equation. Unlike most Werewolf/Mafia variants, there’s only one Night phase in which all the characters play their abilities, half of them being some variant of exchange other players’ cards—stranger yet, the titular wolves don’t get to kill anyone. After the overly long night phase, what follows is a timed 5-minute Day phase at the end of which the players must decide who’s the wolf among them. In theory, this setup should drop you right at the heart of the social deduction experience, but the actual game is everything but that. Without any solid leads, the accusations boil down to flawed, dispassionate deduction at best or blind guessing at worst—no role-playing, no hard evidence, no misdirection, no intrigue, no manipulation, just 5 minutes of noise. Add to that the subpar art style and the less than stellar companion app and you have the one social deduction game I’d rather avoid.

RATING: 7
I had never played Werewolf before and didn't have a lot of interest in it due to the theme, play time, and player elimination.  However, I was really interested in the "One Night Ultimate Werewolf" and "Inquisition" versions after having seen videos for them.  The restricted play time and lack of player elimination are what appealed to me for both games.  I finally got to play "One Night Ultimate Werewolf" a couple times and had fun.  The game plays quickly, yet seems to capture the spirit of the original game.  The app really helps with the game setup and a variable discussion time can be configured.  In addition, some of the characters used can be switched for others for a particular game.  Based on the comments and participation from others playing, it seems that that the game experience does depend on the people playing it.  Even so, it was still fun  and look forward to playing it again.

There are certain combinations of cards that make it almost impossible to win as a werewolf. I think having multiple villagers gives werewolves a fighting chance. If you stick with one of each role you really limit the lies you can tell.

I play it with a group of 5 around a small table. It's the perfect size for moving cards around without anyone noticing. Having more than 5-6 seems like it would become difficult to do any stealthy exchanges and having someone sit out to do the exchanges may not eliminate the issue.

RATING: 6
------------------------------------
Expansions: Daybreak

Probably my favourite social deduction game - You get enough information to make reasonable deductions and it has a locked timer so people can't talk for so long that they bore people into admitting they're a traitor (Which is how I often feel in other similar games, like the Resistance).

The biggest flaw in the game is the lack of method to create predetermined setups - It's very easy to break the balance of information (Either making it so you can pretty irrefutably point out the traitor, or such that no solid information exists and its' pretty much a guess). It's a big shame that they (afaik) have never made a generator in the app that creates well(ish) balanced game compositions.

The other issue is that I've realized how uncomfortable real time/social deduction games make me feel in general, which is why this gets a low rating despite the fact that I actually have a high opinion of the game.
