=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
RATING IN BRIEF:
- For me: 3
- For it's target audience (people who actually like Werewolf mechanics): 8+
- Average: 6ish

I am not a fan of Werewolf: the few games I've played were long and painful, with me sitting there most of the time (having been lynched early on), BORED. But this version has been getting a lot of buzz, and promised to be very very quick so I had to give it a fair shake.

2 plays (7er) and my suspicions are confirmed. This game is quick, but it's still Werewolf :yuk:. And the biggest reason I don't like the game is not for the length (I prefer longer games) or player elimination (although true, I don't like that aspect either); it's because it involves at least 2 skills I lack, and have little interest (or ability?) in acquiring:
- negotiation: convincing people to do stuff. While a great life skill, I just don't want to do it. For example, I've grown very weary of having to convince people that I'm actually not winning something, and they ought to be attacking someone else!
- people-reading: figuring out when someone is lying. That's another life skill that would be nice to have, but I just can't do it! Say what you mean, and mean what you say -- I don't want to have to figure out what you [i]actually[/i] mean!

However, for people who enjoy Werewolf, this game would probably be a real winner! It still has the core elements of the game, albeit with some chaos from the characters in the Ultimate version of the game, but each game is compressed to just 10-15 minutes!

But it's not for me!

[b]--- Summary ---[/b]
A bunch of character cards are distributed randomly, one per player. Then, everyone puts their card in a circle in the center, with some extra cards in the center. Everyone closes their eyes, then someone calls out every character in the game, in order (there's an app for that). When you're called, you act based on your character. There are a variety of powers, for example:
- look at a card
- trade any 2 cards
- copy another power

After every card has been called, everyone opens their eyes and the discussion begins. When everyone is ready, simultaneously point to a person; the player with the most votes is lynched. If the Werewolf is lynched, the Villagers win; otherwise, the Werewolf does. Of course, some characters modify this (e.g., if they're pointed to, they can kill someone else; or if they're killed, they win instead). And since there are some extra cards in the center, it's possible that NO ONE is a Werewolf; Villagers only win if they figure that out and decide not to kill anybody! 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

If you have 6 people or so and don't know what to do and this game is around I would highly suggest it. The Tanner in particular is a genius addition.

Werewolf games are just plain bad and this one removes the one somewhat intriguing part of Ultimate Werewolf, the social party structure.  This game is a single round of Werewolf using some of the roles from the Ultimate package's selection, that's it.

I was introduced to this game as a Werewolf game I would probably like because there was actual deduction involved...buuuuut not really.  Sure, some of the roles allow you to look at other players roles and get some information but others just randomize the whole thing up again.  And if you don't have any special role or you have a stupid role like the drunk who switches his role for a random one without looking at it you are still left with no information and just guessing who is or isn't lying when deciding who to kill.

Not to mention that the two games of this I played, neither had any Werewolves in it...we win...I guess.  Super fun (insert sarcasm here)!  Not only is this not the one Werewolf game I actually enjoy, it is one of the worst I've ever played next to Inquisition.

RATING: 9
This is a direct Werewolf/The Resistance/2R1B* competitor as it has the same team-based play and free form structure but this only takes 10 minutes and it is fantastic. Not 10 minute filler fantastic, BGG Top 100 fantastic.

It is an eclectic mix of puzzle, deduction, bluffing and timing that come together in an awesome  way that provides better opportunities for logical deduction. Go and print out the rules and scribble on some cards so you can play it today. And set aside that Christmas gift card because you don't want to be caught short when it is released.

--

I'll nitpick two issues. 
Being the Werewolves is hard especially with the hunter in play. You can't just be coy or talk BS, you need to be on your A game to win. Even more so if the tanner and/or minion aren't playing well.
The other is that the setup process that is annoying with 8+ players crowding around a table but also requires noise to be made to hide the nightime activities effectively.

*You could also make comparisons to Coup, Citadels or Love Letter for their shorter play times but the individual victors, turn structure, resources and a reduced focus on talking/bluffing give those games a completely different flavour to this.

RATING: 6.5
I'm not a fan of [thing=41114][/thing] or [thing=925][/thing], so I didn't expect much from ONUW. I don't like games that are mostly about lying and just trying to guess who is lying without many data points to inform your decision.  ONUW pretty much falls into that camp.  Most of our games tended to be either totally solved because someone was caught in a lie or a total crapshoot because nobody was caught in a lie.  So the strategy seemed to be to reveal as little info as possible, because that info can only be used against you.

So I didn't find the strategy to be particularly enjoyable, but at least the game played quickly and it was always fun flipping over the cards to see who was whom and which cards got switched.  I'll also give it credit for playing decently at a small player count.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
I'd never played any other version of werewolf before... but I've played The Resistance so I understood the basic mechanic fairly well.  From what I understand this differs from the regular werewolf in that it's only a single round, and everybody picks someone to die, instead of voting on a single person.

This was really fun.  It's more of a party game with a lot of craziness involved.  It's a lot of deduction and bluffing where some of the players aren't sure who they are and others are convinced they're someone they're not.

We played with the free iOS app, which kept track of which roles were in play, gave all the instructions on who should do what when, and timed the game.  The app was pretty sharp and took all the bookkeeping out of the game. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
[thing=147949][/thing] works, mostly, like the regular [thing=925][/thing], with one clear difference: everything happens in a single night.

Some of the roles present in the games are still the same: the Werewolves (they don't kill anyone, however, but the village still wants to find them), the Hunter (if killed, can kill someone else), the Seer (can look at someone else role, or look two of the ones out the game), the Tanner (wants to die, and, if killed, wins alone the game), and so on. But, more important, are the new roles: like the Robber, that trades his role for the one of other player; the Troublemaker, that trades the roles between two other players; the Drunk, that trades his role for one of the center of the table, without looking at his new role; the Insomniac, who sees his role at the end of the night; etc. These roles are designed to insert a high level of uncertainty into the whole situation, and, if that wasn't enough, there are always three roles that stay "out" of the game, in the center of the table, so players don't know exactly what is in the game and what isn't, even if they know all the roles that are beign used in the play.

Therefore, you might have started the game as a Werewolf, but, after the Troublemaker changing roles, you became the Drunk, so, during the day, you will act as a Werewolf, trying to not beign caught and maybe defending your fellow Werewolf, only to discover, in the reveal of the roles, that if you succeeded, you actually lost with the rest of the village!

Basically, the few sure thing the game allows are the roles you see during the night (but you can't be sure if the roles you saw remain with the same persons) and the Insomniac is the port in the storm, as if she is in the game, the player will definitely knows what he is at the end of the night, and this could be key, both for the village and for the werewolves. This is true because, even if players have their roles changed, they will do the actions, at the proper times, related to the ones they saw at the start of the night. So, for istance, say you saw that, at the star of the night, you were the Drunk. During the night, the Robber exchanged his role for yours. Still, when the Drunk is called, you will do the Drunk action, changing your role (now, the Robber) for one at the center of the table, even if you aren't really the Drunk anymore.

The goal of the village is to find one of the Werewolves, and of the Werewolves is to make the village pick anyone else. The Tanner can win alone if he is the one chosen to be killed.

If I had any doubt that this shortened version of [thing=925][/thing] would work, it was completely left behind. [thing=147949][/thing] is fun, chaotic, fast and loud. The only bothersome part is the phase in wich everyone "sleeps" with their eyes closed, as players are called, in the order of the roles, to execute the actions of them. Certainly isn't a fun part, and the more roles you have (i.e: the more players), the longer this phase will take to end. However, the next phase, even if limited in 5 minutes (or maybe [i]because[/i] of this), generates such a fun time, with wild discussions and accusations, that it more than compensates for the waiting time.

The game has an app that allows for it to be played without a GM. It is in English only, so not everyone might deal with it easily.

Now, my only "fear" is that [thing=147949][/thing] will replace most of the other party games in my collection.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 4.5
I am a huge fan of The Resistance so I decided to give this one a try as well since its another small and simple social deduction game.  Unfortunately, it is nowhere near as good.  The app that goes with the game is great, it is much more convenient, fun, and accurate to use it instead of saying the script in the instructions (I don't think I could stand the game if it wasn't for the app).  The main problem I have with the game is that, after everyone has looked at their roles and everyone does their actions, nobody knows what their role even is (a lot of the time).  If you were a werewolf before the action phase, you might be a villager now, and vice-versa.  This makes it impossible for anyone to know for sure if what they are saying is helping or hurting their team.  I really don't enjoy not knowing my own role, and that really breaks the game for me.  Some people I've played with really love this game though, and always rave about it.  It can be fun at a party every once in a while but otherwise I'm not a big fan.  At least it is quick.

RATING: 6.5
A good social deduction game.

Components: Game components are functional, sturdy and minimal. I like the art style and the fact that character tokens were provided as helpful reminders. 

Ease of learning/teaching: The game rules and victory conditions are extremely straightforward. The companion app conducts most of the game and simplifies play.

Theme: The theme is commensurate to the light weight of the game. I enjoyed the many quirky characters and their descriptions. 

Gameplay: Plays quickly and raises enough ruckus around the table to make for a good time. Personally, I haven't taken the game seriously enough to employ adequate group manipulation and deductive reasoning, but I will look forward to getting better at reading people and their actions. 

In conclusion, One Night Ultimate Werewolf makes for a great, fun and breezy filler.

RATING: 5

It gave me the exact same feeling as Mascarade. However being pure party games I would mostly play occasionally with non-gamers/new players, it would take more time to explain the game/roles than to play the game.

[+] like the concept, wish it was easier to teach for the intended audience
[-] maybe with more knowledge of the roles you have more ways to go about it, but for the most part I thought the good guys had no reason to lying in the end (villager, seer, thief, troublemaker, etc.) while the werewolves had to gamble a lot in their interventions.

RATING: 5
This is a decent time waster, billed as a game of werewolf that resolves in just one night (round). That's sort of true, but there is neither time nor enough information to be remotely sure of any accusation you might make. Every game comes down to a wild guess between the 2-3 people that have fallen under suspicion.

That gets old pretty quick. There is nowhere near the drama or the comedy that usually springs up when playing the original Werewolf. Then again, the first two or three people that get hung rarely get to enjoy that anyway. If that tendency bothers you, this version of Werewolf might be good for you. I prefer the old way though, as even watching from the sidelines after an early death has usually been incredibly entertaining.

RATING: 7
A fast game in which everyone gets a role. One of the Werewolves or one of the dozen different villigers, each with a special ability.  The game consists of two phases, 
a night and a day phase. During the night everyone closes their eyes and a players take turn "waking up" to perform their special ability. During the day the villigers try to figure out what happened during the night, and who the werewolf is. In the end, players vote on who to lynch. The game uses an app that keeps track of time and tells everyone what to do during the night.

RATING: 8
It's been a little while since I've played The Resistance, probably because I've played it quite a bit and burned out a tiny bit on it. However, I love social deduction games and want to try all of them out, hence my purchase of this game.

I really liked how quickly the game played out and the fact that there's a timer to make sure things are kept tense and fast. I like that the timer app also does the narration because sometimes it's tough to narrate and play the game at the same time. I enjoyed how the roles switched around almost randomly due to roles like the Troublemaker and the Drunk, it keeps things interesting and makes it hard to determine who's doing what.

If there's anything that I don't like it's that you can easily overplay this game to the point where you're burned out on it and more variety would always be better. I see this sticking around for a while and coming to most game nights as a closer.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
First off, you need to know, I don't even like Werewolf.  In fact, I loathe Werewolf.  2-hour+ games and player elimination makes for a horribly boring situation.  I was vehemently opposed to all variations of Werewolf.

Then I played One Night.  This game changes everything.  ONUW is the only deduction game you will ever need.  10-minute games, zero player elimination, and best of all, [u]everyone[/u] has a reason to lie.  One Night is not only Ultimate Werewolf, but also the ultimate filler game, the ultimate party game, and the ultimate deduction game.

If you are even remotely a fan of Werewolf or any party games, this game is a MUST HAVE for you!

RATING: 8.3
I played some Mafia and Werewolf type games as a kid and I like the mind games of flat-out lying that can occur in them. These types of games usually require a really large group, however, and I don't tend to like the mass player elimination that's really essential in these games.

One Night Ultimate Werewolf, however, gives me the same mind games and lies in under 10 minutes without the player elimination. The roles interact deviously with each other and no one really knows if they've won or not until all the tiles are flipped back up. Werewolves that fought so hard during the discussion phase to ensure that the villagers lynched the wrong person find out that they turned out to be a villager! The laughs, wild accusations, and bold-face lying that have come out of my sessions with this game has been simply the best. We've found that it works best for us with 5+ players, but I'm glad that there's still the option to play it with less.
